The described changes\\n25: // are not applied directly, but contain an approximation of the final\\n26: // result that will be completed during apply by resolving any values that\\n27: // cannot be predicted.\\n28: //\\n29: // A plan must always be accompanied by the configuration it was built from,\\n30: // since the plan does not itself include all of the information required to\\n31: // make the changes indicated.\\n32: type Plan struct {\\n33: \\t// Mode is the mode under which this plan was created.\\n34: \\t//\\n35: \\t// This is only recorded to allow for UI differences when presenting plans\\n36: \\t// to the end-user, and so it must not be used to influence apply-time\\n37: \\t// behavior. VariableValues can potentially contain\\n53: \\t// unknown values for a speculative plan, but the variable values must\\n54: \\t// all be known for a plan that will subsequently be applied.\\n55: \\t//\\n56: \\t// ApplyTimeVariables retains the names of any ephemeral variables that were\\n57: \\t// set (non-null) during the planning phase and must therefore be\\n58: \\t// re-supplied by the caller (potentially with different values) during\\n59: \\t// the apply phase. Don't use this to drive any non-cosmetic behavior, especially\\n120: \\t// including anything that would be subject to compatibility constraints.\\n121: \\tRelevantAttributes []globalref.ResourceAttr\\n122: \\n123: \\t// PrevRunState and PriorState both describe the situation that the plan\\n124: \\t// was derived from:\\n125: \\t//\\n126: \\t// PrevRunState is a representation of the outcome of the previous\\n127: \\t// Terraform operation, without any updates from the remote system but\\n128: \\t// potentially including some changes that resulted from state upgrade\\n129: \\t// actions.\\n130: \\t//\\n131: \\t// PriorState is a representation of the current state of remote objects,\\n132: \\t// which will differ from PrevRunState if the \\\"refresh\\\" step returned\\n133: \\t// different data, which might reflect drift.\\n134: \\t//\\n135: \\t// PriorState is the main snapshot we use for actions during apply.\\n136: \\t// PrevRunState is only here so that we can diff PriorState against it in\\n137: \\t// order to report to the user any out-of-band changes we've detected.\\n138: \\tPrevRunState *states.State\\n139: \\tPriorState   *states.State\\n140: \\n141: \\t// ExternalReferences are references that are being made to resources within\\n142: \\t// the plan from external sources.\\n143: \\t//\\n144: \\t// This is never recorded outside of Terraform. It is not written into the\\n145: \\t// binary plan file, and it is not written into the JSON structured outputs.\\n146: \\t// The testing framework never writes the plans out but holds everything in\\n147: \\t// memory as it executes, so there is no need to add any kind of\\n148: \\t// serialization for this field. This does mean that you shouldn't rely on\\n149: \\t// this field existing unless you have just generated the plan.\\n150: \\tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\\n151: \\n152: \\t// Overrides contains the set of overrides that were applied while making\\n153: \\t// this plan. We need to provide the same set of overrides when applying\\n154: \\t// the plan so we preserve them here. As with  ExternalReferences, this is\\n155: \\t// only used by the testing framework and so isn't written into any external\\n156: \\t// representation of the plan.\\n157: \\tOverrides *mocking.Overrides\\n158: \\n159: \\t// Timestamp is the record of truth for when the plan happened.\\n160: \\tTimestamp time.Time\\n161: \\n162: \\t// ProviderFunctionResults stores hashed results from all provider\\n163: \\t// function calls, so that calls during apply can be checked for\\n164: \\t// consistency.\\n165: \\tProviderFunctionResults []providers.FunctionHash\\n166: }\\n167: \\n168: // ProviderAddrs returns a list of all of the provider configuration addresses\\n169: // referenced throughout the receiving plan.\\n170: //\\n171: // The result is de-duplicated so that each m[key]\\n195: \\t}\\n196: \\n197: \\treturn ret\\n198: }\\n199: \\n200: // Backend represents the backend-related configuration and other data as it\\n201: // existed when a plan was created.\\n202: type Backend struct {\\n203: \\t// Type is the type of backend that the plan will apply against.\\n204: \\tType string\\n205: \\n206: \\t// Config is the configuration of the backend, whose schema is The described changes\n25: // are not applied directly, but contain an approximation of the final\n26: // result that will be completed during apply by resolving any values that\n27: // cannot be predicted.\n28: //\n29: // A plan must always be accompanied by the configuration it was built from,\n30: // since the plan does not itself include all of the information required to\n31: // make the changes indicated.\n32: type Plan struct {\n33: \t// Mode is the mode under which this plan was created.\n34: \t//\n35: \t// This is only recorded to allow for UI differences when presenting plans\n36: \t// to the end-user, and so it must not be used to influence apply-time\n37: \t// behavior. VariableValues can potentially contain\n53: \t// unknown values for a speculative plan, but the variable values must\n54: \t// all be known for a plan that will subsequently be applied.\n55: \t//\n56: \t// ApplyTimeVariables retains the names of any ephemeral variables that were\n57: \t// set (non-null) during the planning phase and must therefore be\n58: \t// re-supplied by the caller (potentially with different values) during\n59: \t// the apply phase.
